<p><b>Allah-Rakha Rahman</b> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:A_R_Rahman.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/A_R_Rahman.ogg" title="A R Rahman.ogg">pronunciation</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:A_R_Rahman.ogg" title="File:A R Rahman.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>, born <b>A. S. Dileep Kumar</b>), is an Indian composer, singer-songwriter, music producer, musician and philanthropist. A. R. Rahman's works are noted for integrating <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Eastern classical music</a> with <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a> and traditional orchestral arrangements. Among his <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_A._R._Rahman" title="List of awards and nominations received by A. R. Rahman">awards</a> are two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, a <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">BAFTA Award</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe</a>, four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Film Awards</a>, fifteen <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a> and thirteen <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards_South" title="Filmfare Awards South">Filmfare Awards South</a>. He has been awarded the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Bhushan" title="Padma Bhushan">Padma Bhushan</a>, the third highest civilian award, in 2010 by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, <i>Time</i> included Rahman on its list of <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">the world's most influential people</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The UK-based world-music magazine <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Songlines" title="Songlines">Songlines</a></i> named him one of "Tomorrow's World Music Icons" in August 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>With an in-house studio (<a href="/wiki/Panchathan_Record_Inn_and_AM_Studios" title="Panchathan Record Inn and AM Studios">Panchathan Record Inn</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>), Rahman's film-scoring career began during the early 1990s with the Tamil film <i><a href="/wiki/Roja" title="Roja">Roja</a></i>. Working in <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_India" title="Cinema of India">India's film industries</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_cinema" title="World cinema">international cinema</a> and theatre, Rahman is one of the world's all-time best-selling recording artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richard_Corliss_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Richard_Corliss-9">[9]</a></sup> In a notable two-decade career, he has been acclaimed for redefining contemporary Indian film music and contributing to the success of several films. Rahman has become a notable humanitarian and philanthropist, donating and raising money for a number of causes and charities.</p>
<p>Rahman's body of work for film and stage has given him the nickname of "the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozart" title="Mozart">Mozart</a> of Madras", and Tamil commentators and fans call him <i>Isai Puyal</i> (English: the Musical Storm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg"><img alt="Two smiling men holding a record award" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="2338" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg/220px-AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg/330px-AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg/440px-AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AR_Rahman_Shashi_Gopal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rahman (left) receiving a platinum award at the MagnaSound Awards; MagnaSound released his first film soundtrack, <i><a href="/wiki/Roja" title="Roja">Roja</a></i>, in 1992.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rahman was born in Chennai, Tamil Nadu, India. His father, <a href="/wiki/R._K._Shekhar" title="R. K. Shekhar">R. K. Shekhar</a>, was a film-score composer and conductor for <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema" title="Tamil cinema">Tamil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malayalam_cinema" title="Malayalam cinema">Malayalam films</a>; Rahman assisted his father in the studio, playing the keyboard.</p>
<p>After his father's death when Rahman was nine years old, the rental of his father's musical equipment provided his family's income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Early_life_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Early_life-11">[11]</a></sup> Raised by his mother, Kareema (born Kashturi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interview_with_Times_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Interview_with_Times-12">[12]</a></sup> Rahman was a keyboard player and arranger for bands such as Roots (with childhood friend and percussionist <a href="/wiki/Sivamani" title="Sivamani">Sivamani</a>, John Anthony, <a href="/wiki/Suresh_Peters" title="Suresh Peters">Suresh Peters</a>, JoJo and Raja)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARR_bio_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARR_bio-13">[13]</a></sup> and founded the Chennai-based rock group Nemesis Avenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>He mastered the keyboard, piano, synthesizer, <a href="/wiki/Pump_organ" title="Pump organ">harmonium</a> and guitar, and was particularly interested in the synthesizer because it was the "ideal combination of music and technology".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rahman began his early musical training under <a href="/wiki/Master_Dhanraj" title="Master Dhanraj">Master Dhanraj</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spotlight_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-spotlight-17">[17]</a></sup> and at age 11 began playing in the orchestra of Malayalam composer (and close friend of his father) <a href="/wiki/M._K._Arjunan" title="M. K. Arjunan">M. K. Arjunan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MK_Arjunan_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-MK_Arjunan-18">[18]</a></sup> He soon began working with other composers, such as <a href="/wiki/M._S._Viswanathan" title="M. S. Viswanathan">M. S. Viswanathan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilaiyaraaja" title="Ilaiyaraaja">Ilaiyaraaja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pasupuleti_Ramesh_Naidu" title="Pasupuleti Ramesh Naidu">Ramesh Naidu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raj-Koti" title="Raj-Koti">Raj-Koti</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spotlight_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-spotlight-17">[17]</a></sup> accompanied <a href="/wiki/Zakir_Hussain_(musician)" title="Zakir Hussain (musician)">Zakir Hussain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kunnakudi_Vaidyanathan" title="Kunnakudi Vaidyanathan">Kunnakudi Vaidyanathan</a> and <a href="/wiki/L._Shankar" title="L. Shankar">L. Shankar</a> on world tours and obtained a scholarship from <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College_London" title="Trinity College London">Trinity College London</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinity_College_of_Music" title="Trinity College of Music">Trinity College of Music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interview_with_Times_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Interview_with_Times-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Studying in Chennai, Rahman graduated with a diploma in <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">Western classical music</a> from the school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPost._19-0"><a href="#cite_note-WaPost.-19">[19]</a></sup> Rahman was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Qadiriyya" title="Qadiriyya">Qadiri</a> <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> when his younger sister was seriously ill in 1984. His mother was a practicing Hindu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dwan_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-dwan-20">[20]</a></sup> He converted to Islam with other members of his family in 1989 at age 23, changing his name from R. S. Dileep Kumar to Allah Rakha Rahman (A. R. Rahman).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Interview_with_Times_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Interview_with_Times-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahmanrs_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rahmanrs-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtracks">Soundtracks</span></h3>
<p>Rahman initially composed scores for documentaries and jingles for advertisements and <a href="/wiki/Television_in_India" title="Television in India">Indian television</a> channels. In 1987 Rahman, then still known as Dileep, composed jingles for a line of watches introduced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hyderabad_Allwyn_Limited" title="Hyderabad Allwyn Limited">Allwyn</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> He also arranged the jingles for some advertisements that went on to become very popular, including the popular jingle for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Titan_Watches" title="Titan Watches">Titan Watches</a>, in which he used the theme from <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._25_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 25 (Mozart)">Mozart's Symphony no.25</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sudhishkamath_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-sudhishkamath-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thehindu.com_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-thehindu.com-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1992, he was approached by director <a href="/wiki/Mani_Ratnam" title="Mani Ratnam">Mani Ratnam</a> to compose the score and soundtrack for his Tamil film, <i><a href="/wiki/Roja" title="Roja">Roja</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-internationalrahman_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-internationalrahman-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rahman's film career began in 1992 when he started <a href="/wiki/Panchathan_Record_Inn_and_AM_Studios" title="Panchathan Record Inn and AM Studios">Panchathan Record Inn</a>, a recording and mixing studio in his backyard. It would become the most-advanced recording studio in India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-internationalrahman_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-internationalrahman-26">[26]</a></sup> and arguably one of Asia's most sophisticated and high-tech studios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Cinematographer <a href="/wiki/Santosh_Sivan" title="Santosh Sivan">Santosh Sivan</a> signed Rahman for the <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Yodha_(1992_film)" title="Yodha (1992 film)">Yodha</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Mohanlal" title="Mohanlal">Mohanlal</a> starrer directed by Sivan's brother <a href="/wiki/Sangeeth_Sivan" title="Sangeeth Sivan">Sangeeth Sivan</a> that released in September 1992.</p>
<p>The following year, Rahman received the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">Rajat Kamal</a> (Silver Lotus) award for best music director at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Film Awards</a> for <i>Roja</i>. The films' score was critically and commercially successful in its original and dubbed versions, led by the innovative theme "<a href="/wiki/Roja_(soundtrack)" title="Roja (soundtrack)">Chinna Chinna Aasai</a>". Rahman followed this with successful scores and songs for <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema" title="Tamil cinema">Tamil–language films</a> for the Chennai film industry, including Ratnam's politically-charged <i><a href="/wiki/Bombay_(film)" title="Bombay (film)">Bombay</a></i>, the urban <i><a href="/wiki/Kadhalan" title="Kadhalan">Kadhalan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Thiruda_Thiruda" title="Thiruda Thiruda">Thiruda Thiruda</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/S._Shankar" title="S. Shankar">S. Shankar</a>'s debut film <i><a href="/wiki/Gentleman_(1993_film)" title="Gentleman (1993 film)">Gentleman</a></i> (with its popular dance song, "<a href="/wiki/Chikku_Bukku_Rayile" title="Chikku Bukku Rayile">Chikku Bukku Rayile</a>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Rahman collaborated with director <a href="/wiki/P._Bharathiraja" title="P. Bharathiraja">Bharathiraaja</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Kizhakku_Cheemayile" title="Kizhakku Cheemayile">Kizhakku Cheemayile</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Karuththamma" title="Karuththamma">Karuththamma</a></i>, producing successful Tamil rural folk-inspired film songs; he also composed for <a href="/wiki/K._Balachander" title="K. Balachander">K. Balachander</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Duet_(1994_film)" title="Duet (1994 film)">Duet</a></i>, which had some memorable Saxophone themes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The 1995 film <i><a href="/wiki/Indira_(film)" title="Indira (film)">Indira</a></i> and romantic comedies <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Romeo" title="Mr. Romeo">Mr. Romeo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Love_Birds_(1996_film)" title="Love Birds (1996 film)">Love Birds</a></i> also drew attention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rahman attracted a Japanese audience with <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muthu_(film)" title="Muthu (film)">Muthu</a>'</i>s success there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muthunoborderss_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-muthunoborderss-38">[38]</a></sup> His soundtracks are known in the Tamil Nadu film industry and abroad for his versatility in combining Western <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>, Carnatic and Tamil traditional and folk-music traditions, <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> and rock music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bombay_(soundtrack)" title="Bombay (soundtrack)">soundtrack for <i>Bombay</i></a> sold 12 million copies worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-release_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-release-43">[43]</a></sup> and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bombay_Theme" title="Bombay Theme">Bombay Theme</a>" would later reappear in his soundtrack for <a href="/wiki/Deepa_Mehta" title="Deepa Mehta">Deepa Mehta</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Fire_(1996_film)" title="Fire (1996 film)">Fire</a></i> and a number of compilations and other media. It was featured in the 2002 Palestinian film <i><a href="/wiki/Divine_Intervention_(film)" title="Divine Intervention (film)">Divine Intervention</a></i> and the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Cage" title="Nicolas Cage">Nicolas Cage</a> film, <i><a href="/wiki/Lord_of_War" title="Lord of War">Lord of War</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Rangeela_(film)" title="Rangeela (film)">Rangeela</a></i>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Ram_Gopal_Varma" title="Ram Gopal Varma">Ram Gopal Varma</a>, was Rahman's <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Successful scores and songs for <i><a href="/wiki/Dil_Se.." title="Dil Se..">Dil Se..</a></i> and the percussive <i><a href="/wiki/Taal_(film)" title="Taal (film)">Taal</a></i> followed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-understandingaf_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-understandingaf-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufi mysticism</a> inspired "<a href="/wiki/Chaiyya_Chaiyya" title="Chaiyya Chaiyya">Chaiyya Chaiyya</a>" from the former film and "Zikr" from his soundtrack album for <i><a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose:_The_Forgotten_Hero" title="Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose: The Forgotten Hero">Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose: The Forgotten Hero</a></i> (which featured elaborate orchestral and choral arrangements).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahmanrs_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rahmanrs-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rahman's soundtrack album for the Chennai production <i>Minsaara Kanavu</i> won him his second National Film Award for Best Music Direction and a <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Music_Director_%E2%80%93_Tamil" title="Filmfare Award for Best Music Director – Tamil">South FilmFare Award for Best Music Direction in a Tamil film</a> in 1997, the latter setting a record of six consecutive wins; he later went on to win the award three consecutive additional times. The musical cues in the soundtrack albums for <i><a href="/wiki/Sangamam" title="Sangamam">Sangamam</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Iruvar" title="Iruvar">Iruvar</a></i> used Carnatic vocals, the <a href="/wiki/Veena" title="Veena">veena</a>, rock guitar and jazz.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archat98_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-archat98-47">[47]</a></sup> During the 2000s, Rahman composed scores and popular songs for <a href="/wiki/Rajiv_Menon" title="Rajiv Menon">Rajiv Menon</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Kandukondain_Kandukondain" title="Kandukondain Kandukondain">Kandukondain Kandukondain</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaipayuthey_(film)" title="Alaipayuthey (film)">Alaipayuthey</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Ashutosh_Gowariker" title="Ashutosh Gowariker">Ashutosh Gowariker</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Swades" title="Swades">Swades</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rang_De_Basanti" title="Rang De Basanti">Rang De Basanti</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and songs with Hindustani motifs for 2005's <i><a href="/wiki/Water_(2005_film)" title="Water (2005 film)">Water</a></i>. Rahman has worked with Indian poets and lyricists such as <a href="/wiki/Javed_Akhtar" title="Javed Akhtar">Javed Akhtar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulzar" title="Gulzar">Gulzar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vairamuthu" title="Vairamuthu">Vairamuthu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vaali_(poet)" title="Vaali (poet)">Vaali</a>, and has produced commercially-successful soundtracks with directors <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_directed_by_Mani_Ratnam_featuring_A._R._Rahman" title="List of films directed by Mani Ratnam featuring A. R. Rahman">Mani Ratnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/S._Shankar" title="S. Shankar">S. Shankar</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Gentleman_(1993_film)" title="Gentleman (1993 film)">Gentleman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Kadhalan" title="Kadhalan">Kadhalan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Indian_(1996_film)" title="Indian (1996 film)">Indian</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jeans_(film)" title="Jeans (film)">Jeans</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mudhalvan" title="Mudhalvan">Mudhalvan</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nayak_(2001_film)" title="Nayak (2001 film)">Nayak</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Boys_(2003_film)" title="Boys (2003 film)">Boys</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sivaji_(film)" title="Sivaji (film)">Sivaji</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Enthiran" title="Enthiran">Enthiran</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2005 Rahman expanded his Panchathan Record Inn studio by establishing <a href="/wiki/Panchathan_Record_Inn_and_AM_Studios" title="Panchathan Record Inn and AM Studios">AM Studios</a> in Kodambakkam, Chennai, creating the most cutting-edge studio in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahmanammix_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rahmanammix-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The following year he launched his own music label, KM Music,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> with his score for <i><a href="/wiki/Sillunu_Oru_Kaadhal" title="Sillunu Oru Kaadhal">Sillunu Oru Kaadhal</a>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Rahman scored the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" title="Standard Mandarin">Mandarin</a>-language film <i><a href="/wiki/Warriors_of_Heaven_and_Earth" title="Warriors of Heaven and Earth">Warriors of Heaven and Earth</a></i> in 2003 after researching and using <a href="/wiki/Music_of_China" title="Music of China">Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gagaku" title="Gagaku">Japanese classical</a> music,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> and won the <a href="/wiki/Just_Plain_Folks_Music_Organization" title="Just Plain Folks Music Organization">Just Plain Folks Music Award For Best Music Album</a> for his score for 2006's <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Varalaru_(film)" title="Varalaru (film)">Varalaru (God Father)</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> He co-scored <a href="/wiki/Shekhar_Kapur" title="Shekhar Kapur">Shekhar Kapur</a>'s first British film, <i><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth:_The_Golden_Age" title="Elizabeth: The Golden Age">Elizabeth: The Golden Age</a></i>, in 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> and received a Best Composer <a href="/wiki/Asian_Film_Awards" title="Asian Film Awards">Asian Film Award</a> nomination at the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_International_Film_Festival" title="Hong Kong International Film Festival">Hong Kong International Film Festival</a> for his <i><a href="/wiki/Jodhaa_Akbar" title="Jodhaa Akbar">Jodhaa Akbar</a></i> score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Rahman's music has been sampled for other scores in India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> appearing in <i><a href="/wiki/Inside_Man" title="Inside Man">Inside Man</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lord_of_War" title="Lord of War">Lord of War</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Divine_Intervention_(film)" title="Divine Intervention (film)">Divine Intervention</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Accidental_Husband" title="The Accidental Husband">The Accidental Husband</a>.</i></p>
<p>His score for his first Hollywood film, the 2009 comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Couples_Retreat" title="Couples Retreat">Couples Retreat</a></i>, won the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Music,_Inc." title="Broadcast Music, Inc.">BMI</a> London Award for Best Score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Broadcast_Music_Inc_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Broadcast_Music_Inc-59">[59]</a></sup> Rahman's music for 2008's <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i> won a Golden Globe and two Academy Awards (a first for an Asian), and the songs "<a href="/wiki/Jai_Ho_(song)" title="Jai Ho (song)">Jai Ho</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/O..._Saya" title="O... Saya">O... Saya</a>" from its soundtrack were internationally successful. His music on 2008's Bollywood <i><a href="/wiki/Jaane_Tu..._Ya_Jaane_Na" title="Jaane Tu... Ya Jaane Na">Jaane Tu... Ya Jaane Na</a></i> was popular with Indian youth; that year, his score and songs for <i><a href="/wiki/Jodhaa_Akbar" title="Jodhaa Akbar">Jodhaa Akbar</a></i> won critical acclaim, a Best Composer Asian Film Award nomination and <a href="/wiki/IIFA_Award_for_Best_Music_Director" title="IIFA Award for Best Music Director">IIFA awards for best music direction and score</a>.</p>
<p>In 2010, Rahman composed the original score and songs for the romantic <i><a href="/wiki/Vinnaithaandi_Varuvaayaa_(soundtrack)" title="Vinnaithaandi Varuvaayaa (soundtrack)">Vinnaithaandi Varuvaayaa</a></i>, the sci-fi romance <i><a href="/wiki/Enthiran_(soundtrack)" title="Enthiran (soundtrack)">Enthiran</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Boyle" title="Danny Boyle">Danny Boyle</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/127_Hours:_Music_from_the_Motion_Picture" title="127 Hours: Music from the Motion Picture">127 Hours</a></i>, composing for the <a href="/wiki/Imtiaz_Ali_(director)" title="Imtiaz Ali (director)">Imtiaz Ali</a> musical <i><a href="/wiki/Rockstar_(soundtrack)" title="Rockstar (soundtrack)">Rockstar</a></i>; the latter's soundtrack was a critical and commercial success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rockstar.27s_rocking_on_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rockstar.27s_rocking_on-60">[60]</a></sup> In 2012 Rahman composed for <i><a href="/wiki/Ekk_Deewana_Tha_(soundtrack)" title="Ekk Deewana Tha (soundtrack)">Ekk Deewana Tha</a></i> and the American drama <i><a href="/wiki/People_Like_Us_(film)" title="People Like Us (film)">People Like Us</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> and collaborated with director <a href="/wiki/Yash_Chopra" title="Yash Chopra">Yash Chopra</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Jab_Tak_Hai_Jaan_(soundtrack)" title="Jab Tak Hai Jaan (soundtrack)">Jab Tak Hai Jaan</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> all were positively received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> By the end of the year his music for Mani Ratnam's <i><a href="/wiki/Kadal_(soundtrack)" title="Kadal (soundtrack)">Kadal</a></i> was critically acclaimed, and the album topped the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes India</a> chart for December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In 2013, Rahman had two releases: <i><a href="/wiki/Raanjhanaa_(soundtrack)" title="Raanjhanaa (soundtrack)">Raanjhanaa</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Maryan_(soundtrack)" title="Maryan (soundtrack)">Maryan</a></i>. Both were successful, with the former nominated for a number of awards<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59th_Idea_Filmfare_Awards_Nominations_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-59th_Idea_Filmfare_Awards_Nominations-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GIMA_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-GIMA-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bas_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-bas-67">[67]</a></sup> and the latter the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes India</a> Tamil Album of 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>The year 2014 was one of the busiest years for Rahman, with him claiming to have worked in 12 films in various languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> While his first release for the year was the <a href="/wiki/Imtiaz_Ali_(director)" title="Imtiaz Ali (director)">Imtiaz Ali</a>'s road movie <i><a href="/wiki/Highway_(2014_Hindi_film)" title="Highway (2014 Hindi film)">Highway</a></i> which garnered positive reviews, his very next release was the performance captured animation film <i><a href="/wiki/Kochadaiiyaan" title="Kochadaiiyaan">Kochadaiiyaan</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Rajinikanth" title="Rajinikanth">Rajinikanth</a> starrer directed by <a href="/wiki/Soundarya_Rajinikanth" title="Soundarya Rajinikanth">Soundarya Rajinikanth</a>. The film's score and soundtrack garnered huge critical appraise with its score being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long-listed" title="Long-listed">long-listed</a> at the forthcoming <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> His next were the scores for the two back to back Hollywood films, <i><a href="/wiki/Million_Dollar_Arm" title="Million Dollar Arm">Million Dollar Arm</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Hundred_Foot_Journey" title="The Hundred Foot Journey">The Hundred Foot Journey</a></i>, both of which got into the contended list for the original score category nomination at the Oscars.</p>
<p>This was followed by the highly successful soundtrack album for the period drama <i><a href="/wiki/Kaaviya_Thalaivan_(2014_film)" title="Kaaviya Thalaivan (2014 film)">Kaaviya Thalaivan</a></i> teaming up with director <a href="/wiki/Vasanthabalan" title="Vasanthabalan">Vasanthabalan</a> for the first time. His next release was <a href="/wiki/S._Shankar" title="S. Shankar">Shankar</a>'s supernatural thriller <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_(2014_film)" title="I (2014 film)">I</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/K._S._Ravikumar" title="K. S. Ravikumar">K. S. Ravikumar</a>'s period action film <i><a href="/wiki/Lingaa" title="Lingaa">Lingaa</a></i>, both of which were highly acclaimed and appreciated upon release.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_scores">Background scores</span></h3>
<p>Apart from successful soundtracks, he is also known for highly acclaimed background scores and is considered, one of the finest background-score composers in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biography_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biography-71">[71]</a></sup> His background scores are often characterised by the usage of subtle orchestration and ambient sounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biography_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Biography-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trained in western classical music, he often employs contemporary instruments such as Guitars, Cello, Flute, Strings, Keyboard, Finger board, Harpejji, Santoor and traditional Indian instruments such as Shehnai, Sitar, Mrudangam, Veenai &amp; Tabla to create scores.</p>
<p>Apart from getting high critical appreciations, several of Rahman's background scores have earned him many prestigious awards ranging from Academy awards to Filmfare awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biography_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-Biography-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Some of the films which fetched him appreciations for background scores include <i><a href="/wiki/Roja" title="Roja">Roja</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bombay_(film)" title="Bombay (film)">Bombay</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Iruvar" title="Iruvar">Iruvar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Minsara_Kanavu" title="Minsara Kanavu">Minsara Kanavu</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dil_Se.." title="Dil Se..">Dil Se..</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Taal_(film)" title="Taal (film)">Taal</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lagaan" title="Lagaan">Lagaan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_Bhagat_Singh" title="The Legend of Bhagat Singh">The Legend of Bhagat Singh</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Swades" title="Swades">Swades</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rang_De_Basanti" title="Rang De Basanti">Rang De Basanti</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Netaji_Subhas_Chandra_Bose:_The_Forgotten_Hero" title="Netaji Subhas Chandra Bose: The Forgotten Hero">Bose: The Forgotten Hero</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Guru_(2007_film)" title="Guru (2007 film)">Guru</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jodhaa_Akbar" title="Jodhaa Akbar">Jodhaa Akbar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Raavanan" title="Raavanan">Raavanan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Vinnaithaandi_Varuvaayaa" title="Vinnaithaandi Varuvaayaa">Vinnaithaandi Varuvaayaa</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rockstar_(2011_film)" title="Rockstar (2011 film)">Rockstar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Enthiran" title="Enthiran">Enthiran</a></i> ,<i><a href="/wiki/Kadal_(2013_film)" title="Kadal (2013 film)">Kadal</a></i> , <i><a href="/wiki/Kochadaiiyaan" title="Kochadaiiyaan">Kochadaiiyaan</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/I_(film)" title="I (film)">I</a></i>. Among his Hollywood scores, <i><a href="/wiki/Warriors_of_Heaven_and_Earth" title="Warriors of Heaven and Earth">Warriors of Heaven and Earth</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/127_Hours" title="127 Hours">127 Hours</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Million_Dollar_Arm" title="Million Dollar Arm">Million Dollar Arm</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hundred-Foot_Journey_(film)" title="The Hundred-Foot Journey (film)">The Hundred-Foot Journey</a></i> received rave reviews. A. R. Rahman received two <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i> and two <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> nominations for <i><a href="/wiki/127_Hours" title="127 Hours">127 Hours</a></i>. Recently, his scores for <i><a href="/wiki/Kochadaiiyaan" title="Kochadaiiyaan">Kochadaiiyaan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Million_Dollar_Arm" title="Million Dollar Arm">Million Dollar Arm</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hundred-Foot_Journey_(film)" title="The Hundred-Foot Journey (film)">The Hundred-Foot Journey</a></i> have been nominated in the long list released by <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_and_other_projects">Performing and other projects</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg"><img alt="Male singer with female singers and dancers" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2925" data-file-width="4220" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg/220px-Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg/330px-Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg/440px-Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert_2010_A.R._Rahman_IMG_7174.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rahman at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize_Concert" title="Nobel Peace Prize Concert">Nobel Peace Prize Concert</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rahman has also been involved in <a href="/wiki/A._R._Rahman_discography#Albums" title="A. R. Rahman discography">non-film projects</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Vande_Mataram_(album)" title="Vande Mataram (album)">Vande Mataram</a></i>, an album of original compositions released for India's 50th anniversary of its independence in 1997,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahmanbiovm_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rahmanbiovm-77">[77]</a></sup> is one of India's bestselling non-film albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> He followed it with an album for the <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Bala" title="Bharat Bala">Bharat Bala</a>–directed video <i><a href="/wiki/Jana_Gana_Mana_Video" title="Jana Gana Mana Video">Jana Gana Mana</a></i>, a collection of performances by leading exponents and artists of <a href="/wiki/Indian_classical_music" title="Indian classical music">Indian classical music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Rahman has written advertising jingles and orchestrations for athletic events, television and Internet media, documentaries and short films,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> frequently using the Czech Film Orchestra and the Chennai Strings Orchestra.</p>
<p>In 1999, Rahman partnered with choreographers <a href="/wiki/Shobana" title="Shobana">Shobana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prabhu_Deva" title="Prabhu Deva">Prabhu Deva</a> and a Tamil film-dancing troupe to perform with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, Germany at his Michael Jackson and Friends concert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In 2002 he composed the music for his first stage production, <i><a href="/wiki/Bombay_Dreams" title="Bombay Dreams">Bombay Dreams</a></i>, which was commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber">Andrew Lloyd Webber</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The Finnish folk-music band <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4rttin%C3%A4" title="Värttinä">Värttinä</a> collaborated with Rahman on the Toronto production of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(musical)#Toronto_production" title="The Lord of the Rings (musical)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, and in 2004<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lotrrahmanc_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-lotrrahmanc-83">[83]</a></sup> he composed "Raga's Dance" for <a href="/wiki/Vanessa-Mae" title="Vanessa-Mae">Vanessa-Mae</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Choreography_(Vanessa-Mae_album)" title="Choreography (Vanessa-Mae album)">Choreography</a></i> (performed by Mae and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Royal Philharmonic Orchestra">Royal Philharmonic Orchestra</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg"><img alt="Singer and guitarist in front of effects smoke" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1193" data-file-width="2048" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg/220px-A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg/330px-A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg/440px-A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A._R._Rahman_at_Sufi_Concert_in_Dubai.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A. R. Rahman at Sufi Concert in Dubai</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 2004 Rahman has performed three successful world <a href="/wiki/Tours" title="Tours">tours</a> before audiences in Singapore, Australia, Malaysia, <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>, the United Kingdom, Canada, the United States and India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lotrrahmanc_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-lotrrahmanc-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and has been collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Karen_David" title="Karen David">Karen David</a> on her upcoming studio album. A two-disc CD, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Introducing_A._R._Rahman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Introducing A. R. Rahman (page does not exist)">Introducing A. R. Rahman</a></i> (featuring 25 of his Tamil film-score pieces), was released in May 2006<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and his non-film album <i>Connections</i> was released on 12 December 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Rahman performed at a White House <a href="/wiki/State_dinner" title="State dinner">state dinner</a> arranged by US President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> during an official visit by Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a> on 24 November 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> He is one of over 70 artists on "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_World_25_for_Haiti" title="We Are the World 25 for Haiti">We Are the World 25 for Haiti</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Charity_record" title="Charity record">charity single</a> to raise relief funds in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Haiti_earthquake" title="2010 Haiti earthquake">2010 Haiti earthquake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In 2010, Rahman composed "<a href="/wiki/Jai_Jai_Garvi_Gujarat" title="Jai Jai Garvi Gujarat">Jai Jai Garvi Gujarat</a>" in honour of the 50th anniversary of the formation of Gujarat State,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Semmozhiyaana_Thamizh_Mozhiyaam" title="Semmozhiyaana Thamizh Mozhiyaam">Semmozhiyaana Thamizh Mozhiyaam</a>" as part of the <a href="/wiki/World_Classical_Tamil_Conference_2010" title="World Classical Tamil Conference 2010">World Classical Tamil Conference 2010</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and the theme song for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010 Commonwealth Games</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Jiyo_Utho_Bado_Jeeto" title="Jiyo Utho Bado Jeeto">Jiyo Utho Bado Jeeto</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Rahman began his first world tour, (<a href="/wiki/A._R._Rahman_Jai_Ho_Concert:_The_Journey_Home_World_Tour" title="A. R. Rahman Jai Ho Concert: The Journey Home World Tour">A. R. Rahman Jai Ho Concert: The Journey Home World Tour</a>) on 11 June 2010 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nassau_Coliseum" title="Nassau Coliseum">Nassau Coliseum</a> in New York; 16 cities worldwide were scheduled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some of Rahman's notable compositions were performed by the <a href="/wiki/London_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="London Philharmonic Orchestra">London Philharmonic Orchestra</a> in April 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> In February 2011 Rahman collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bolton" title="Michael Bolton">Michael Bolton</a> on Bolton's album, <i><a href="/wiki/Gems_(Michael_Bolton_album)" title="Gems (Michael Bolton album)">Gems – The Duets Collection</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> reworking his "Sajna" from <i><a href="/wiki/Couples_Retreat" title="Couples Retreat">Couples Retreat</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 May 2011 <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jagger" title="Mick Jagger">Mick Jagger</a> announced the formation of a <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a>, <a href="/wiki/SuperHeavy" title="SuperHeavy">SuperHeavy</a>, with <a href="/wiki/David_A._Stewart" title="David A. Stewart">Dave Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joss_Stone" title="Joss Stone">Joss Stone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damian_Marley" title="Damian Marley">Damian Marley</a> and Rahman;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> its <a href="/wiki/SuperHeavy_(album)" title="SuperHeavy (album)">self-titled album</a> was scheduled for release in September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The album would have Jagger singing on Rahman's composition, "Satyameva Jayate" ("The Truth Alone Triumphs").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Filmorchester_Babelsberg" title="Deutsches Filmorchester Babelsberg">Deutsches Filmorchester Babelsberg</a> announced that it would join <a href="/wiki/KM_Music_Conservatory" title="KM Music Conservatory">KM Music Conservatory</a> musicians for a 100-member concert tour of five Indian cities (Germany and India 2011–2012: Infinite Opportunities), performing Rahman's songs. The marked the centennial of Indian cinema and Babelsberg Studio, the world's oldest film studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biography_71-3"><a href="#cite_note-Biography-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Summer 2012 Rahman composed a <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> song for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">London Olympics</a> <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Danny_Boyle" title="Danny Boyle">Danny Boyle</a>, part of a medley showcasing <a href="/wiki/India%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="India–United Kingdom relations">Indian influence in the UK</a>. Indian musician <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilaiyaraja" title="Ilaiyaraja">Ilaiyaraja</a>'s song from the 1981 <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil-language</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Ram_Lakshman" title="Ram Lakshman">Ram Lakshman</a></i> was also chosen for the medley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2012 Rahman and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shekhar_Kapoor" title="Shekhar Kapoor">Shekhar Kapoor</a> launched Qyuki, a networking site which is a platform for story writers to exchange their thoughts. Cisco invested ₹270 million in the startup, giving it a 17-percent share. Qyuki uses Cisco's cloud infrastructure for the site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> On 20 December he released the single "Infinite Love" in English and Hindi, commemorating the last day of the Mayan calendar to spread hope, peace and love. Rahman's 2013 tour, Rahmanishq, was announced on 29 July 2013 in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>. Beginning in Sydney on 24 August, the tour moved to a number of cities in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2016, after a long break A. R. Rahman performed live in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a> and for the first time in <a href="/wiki/Coimbatore" title="Coimbatore">Coimbatore</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Madurai" title="Madurai">Madurai</a>, with a complete Tamil playlist. As the name suggests, <i>Nenje Yezhu</i> (which means rise up) began 2016 with a positive note and with music from the heart. The proceeds of this concert will be used for flood relief in Tamil Nadu and also for creating awareness against cancer, supporting VS Medical Trust outside Chennai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_impact">Musical style and impact</span></h2>
<p>Skilled in Carnatic music, <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">Western</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music" title="Hindustani classical music">Hindustani classical music</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Qawwali" title="Qawwali">Qawwali</a> style of <a href="/wiki/Nusrat_Fateh_Ali_Khan" title="Nusrat Fateh Ali Khan">Nusrat Fateh Ali Khan</a>, Rahman is noted for film songs amalgamating elements of these and other genres, layering instruments from different musical idioms in an improvisational style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahmanrs_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rahmanrs-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Symphonic orchestral themes accompany his scores, occasionally using a <a href="/wiki/Leitmotif" title="Leitmotif">leitmotif</a>. During the 1980s Rahman recorded <a href="/wiki/Monaural" title="Monaural">monaural</a> arrangements in common with his musical predecessors, <a href="/wiki/K._V._Mahadevan" title="K. V. Mahadevan">K. V. Mahadevan</a> and <a href="/wiki/M._S._Viswanathan" title="M. S. Viswanathan">Vishwanathan</a>–<a href="/wiki/T._K._Ramamoorthy" title="T. K. Ramamoorthy">Ramamoorthy</a>. In later years his methodology changed, as he experimented with the fusion of traditional instruments with new electronic sounds and technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahmanrs_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rahmanrs-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rahman's musical interests and outlook originate in his love of experimentation. His compositions have an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Auteur_theory" title="Auteur theory">auteuristic</a> use of <a href="/wiki/Counterpoint" title="Counterpoint">counterpoint</a>, orchestration and the <a href="/wiki/Human_voice" title="Human voice">human voice</a>, melding Indian pop music with a unique <a href="/wiki/Timbre" title="Timbre">timbre</a>, form and instrumentation. With this syncretic style and wide-ranging lyrics, the appeal of Rahman's music crosses classes and cultures in Indian society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wom_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-wom-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>His first soundtrack, for <i><a href="/wiki/Roja" title="Roja">Roja</a></i>, was listed on <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a>'s</i> all-time "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_magazine%27s_%22All-TIME%22_100_best_movies#10_Best_Soundtracks" title="Time magazine's &quot;All-TIME&quot; 100 best movies">10 Best Soundtracks</a>" in 2005. Film critic <a href="/wiki/Richard_Corliss" title="Richard Corliss">Richard Corliss</a> said that the composer's "astonishing debut work parades Rahman's gift for alchemizing outside influences until they are totally Tamil, totally Rahman",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timetop10s_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Timetop10s-111">[111]</a></sup> and his initial global success is attributed to the <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian diaspora</a>. Music producer <a href="/wiki/Ron_Fair" title="Ron Fair">Ron Fair</a> considers Rahman "one of the world's great living composers in any medium".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Director <a href="/wiki/Baz_Luhrmann" title="Baz Luhrmann">Baz Luhrmann</a> said:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I had come to the music of A. R. Rahman through the emotional and haunting score of <i>Bombay</i> and the wit and celebration of <i>Lagaan</i>. But the more of AR's music I encountered the more I was to be amazed at the sheer diversity of styles: from swinging brass bands to triumphant anthems; from joyous pop to West-End musicals. Whatever the style, A. R. Rahman's music always possesses a profound sense of humanity and spirit, qualities that inspire me the most.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charindaa_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-charindaa-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Rahman introduced <a href="/wiki/7.1_surround_sound" title="7.1 surround sound">7.1 surround sound</a> technology to South Indian films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 May 2014 Rahman announced that he has partnered with former Black Eyed Peas’ Will.i.am to recreate an early popular track 'Urvashi Urvashi'. Track is 'Birthday'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_A._R._Rahman" title="List of awards and nominations received by A. R. Rahman">List of awards and nominations received by A. R. Rahman</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg"><img alt="Man sitting on couch, with two Academy Awards on table in front of him" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg/170px-Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg/255px-Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg/340px-Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oscar_Puyal_Rahman.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rahman at his home in Chennai, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rahman was the 1995 recipient of the Mauritius National Award and the Malaysian Award for his contributions to music,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turns_44_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Turns_44-116">[116]</a></sup> and was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier_Award" title="Laurence Olivier Award">Laurence Olivier Award</a> for his first West End production. A four-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards_(India)" title="National Film Awards (India)">National Film Award</a> winner and recipient of six <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu_State_Film_Awards" title="Tamil Nadu State Film Awards">Tamil Nadu State Film Awards</a>, he has fifteen <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a> and thirteen <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards_South" title="Filmfare Awards South">Filmfare Awards South</a> for his music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turns_44_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-Turns_44-116">[116]</a></sup> Rahman has received a <a href="/wiki/Kalaimamani" title="Kalaimamani">Kalaimamani</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Tamil_Nadu" title="Government of Tamil Nadu">Government of Tamil Nadu</a> for excellence in the field of music, musical-achievement awards from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Uttar_Pradesh" title="Government of Uttar Pradesh">governments of Uttar Pradesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Madhya_Pradesh" title="Government of Madhya Pradesh">Madhya Pradesh</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Padma_Shri_Awards_(2000%E2%80%932009)" title="Padma Shri Awards (2000–2009)">Padma Shri</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, he received an award from <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> for his contributions to global music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-arstan06_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-arstan06-118">[118]</a></sup> The following year, Rahman entered the <i><a href="/wiki/Limca_Book_of_Records" title="Limca Book of Records">Limca Book of Records</a></i> as "Indian of the Year for Contribution to Popular Music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> He received the 2008 Lifetime Achievement Award from the <a href="/wiki/Rotary_International" title="Rotary International">Rotary Club of Madras</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> In 2009, for his <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i> score, Rahman won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_Film_Critics_Association_Award" title="Broadcast Film Critics Association Award">Broadcast Film Critics Association Award</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Original Score">Golden Globe Award for Best Original Score</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globes_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-globes-121">[121]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Film_Music" title="BAFTA Award for Best Film Music">BAFTA Award for Best Film Music</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> (<a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Academy Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Score</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a>, the latter shared with <a href="/wiki/Gulzar" title="Gulzar">Gulzar</a>) at the <a href="/wiki/81st_Academy_Awards" title="81st Academy Awards">81st Academy Awards</a>.</p>
<p>He has received honorary doctorates from <a href="/wiki/Middlesex_University" title="Middlesex University">Middlesex University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aligarh_Muslim_University" title="Aligarh Muslim University">Aligarh Muslim University</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anna_University" title="Anna University">Anna University</a> in Chennai and Miami University in Ohio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The composer has won two <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Compilation_Soundtrack_Album_for_a_Motion_Picture,_Television_or_Other_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Compilation Soundtrack Album for a Motion Picture, Television or Other Visual Media">Best Compilation Soundtrack Album</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Song_Written_for_a_Motion_Picture,_Television_or_Other_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Song Written for a Motion Picture, Television or Other Visual Media">Best Song Written for Visual Media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-125">[125]</a></sup> Rahman received the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Bhushan" title="Padma Bhushan">Padma Bhushan</a>, India's third-highest civilian honour, in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>His work in <i><a href="/wiki/127_Hours" title="127 Hours">127 Hours</a></i> won him Golden Globe, BAFTA, and two Academy Award nominations (Best Original Music Score and Best Original Song) in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Rahman is an Honorary Fellow of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinity_College_of_Music" title="Trinity College of Music">Trinity College of Music</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 October 2014 Rahman was awarded an honorary doctorate from <a href="/wiki/Berklee_College_of_Music" title="Berklee College of Music">Berklee College of Music</a> during a concert paying tribute to his music featuring an international cast of students. Upon receiving his award he commented that being honored by Berklee illustrates how his life has come full circle, as at the start of his career, he had planned to study at Berklee before being offered the opportunity to score <i>Roja</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> During his 7 May 2012 acceptance speech of his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honorary_doctorate" title="Honorary doctorate">honorary doctorate</a> from <a href="/wiki/Miami_University" title="Miami University">Miami University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, Rahman mentioned that he received a Christmas card from the family of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> and an invitation to dinner at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> A street was named in his honour in Markham, Ontario, Canada in November 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 October 2015, the government of Seychelles named A. R. Rahman <i>Cultural Ambassador for Seychelles</i> in appreciation of the "invaluable services contributed to enhance Seychelles' Arts and Culture development."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_R_Rahman,Saira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg"><img alt="Man in grey jacket and woman in sari" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="459" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/A_R_Rahman%2CSaira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg/150px-A_R_Rahman%2CSaira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/A_R_Rahman%2CSaira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg/225px-A_R_Rahman%2CSaira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/A_R_Rahman%2CSaira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg/300px-A_R_Rahman%2CSaira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_R_Rahman,Saira_Banu_From_The_Audio_release_of_%27Enthiran_-_The_Robot%27.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rahman and his wife, Saira Banu, at the 2010 soundtrack release of <i><a href="/wiki/Enthiran" title="Enthiran">Enthiran</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rahman is married to Saira Banu and has three children: Khatija, Rahima and Ameen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Ameen has sung "NaNa" from <i><a href="/wiki/Couples_Retreat_(soundtrack)" title="Couples Retreat (soundtrack)">Couples Retreat</a></i>, and Khatija has sung "Pudhiya Manidha" from <i><a href="/wiki/Enthiran_(soundtrack)" title="Enthiran (soundtrack)">Enthiran</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Rahman is the uncle of composer <a href="/wiki/G._V._Prakash_Kumar" title="G. V. Prakash Kumar">G. V. Prakash Kumar</a>, the son of his older sister <a href="/wiki/A._R._Reihana" title="A. R. Reihana">A. R. Reihana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Kumar's first film work was singing on Rahman's "Chikku Bukku Rayile", from his score for 1993's <i>Gentleman</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Reihana's film debut was singing on "Vidai Kodu Engal Naadae" from <i><a href="/wiki/Kannathil_Muthamittal" title="Kannathil Muthamittal">Kannathil Muthamittal</a></i>, and she is a music director. Rahman's younger sister, Fathima, heads his music conservatory in Chennai. The youngest, Ishrath, has a music studio. A.R.Rahman is the co-brother of film actor <a href="/wiki/Rahman_(actor)" title="Rahman (actor)">Rahman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Born Hindu in a Tamil <a href="/wiki/Mudaliar" title="Mudaliar">Mudaliar</a> family,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Dileep Kumar converted to Islam in 1989 and assumed his present name, Rahman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dwan_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-dwan-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talkasia_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-talkasia-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> After the early death of his father, his family experienced difficult times; <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">Sufism</a> influenced his mother who was a practicing Hindu<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dwan_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-dwan-20">[20]</a></sup> and, eventually, his family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-talkasia_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-talkasia-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/81st_Academy_Awards" title="81st Academy Awards">81st Academy Awards</a> ceremony Rahman paid tribute to his mother: "There is a Hindi dialogue, <i>mere pass ma hai</i>, which means 'even if I have got nothing I have my mother here'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> He said, "<i>Ella pughazhum iraivanukke</i>" ("All praise to God" in <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, a translation from the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>) before his speech.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_work">Humanitarian work</span></h2>
<p>Rahman is involved with a number of charitable causes. In 2004 he was appointed global ambassador of the <a href="/wiki/Stop_TB_Partnership" title="Stop TB Partnership">Stop TB Partnership</a>, a <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">WHO</a> project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lotrrahmanc_83-2"><a href="#cite_note-lotrrahmanc-83">[83]</a></sup> Rahman has supported <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a> India and worked with <a href="/wiki/Cat_Stevens" title="Cat Stevens">Yusuf Islam</a> on "Indian Ocean", a song featuring <a href="/wiki/A-ha" title="A-ha">a-ha</a> keyboard player <a href="/wiki/Magne_Furuholmen" title="Magne Furuholmen">Magne Furuholmen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Travis_(band)" title="Travis (band)">Travis</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Neil_Primrose_(musician)" title="Neil Primrose (musician)">Neil Primrose</a>. Proceeds from the song went to help orphans in <a href="/wiki/Banda_Aceh" title="Banda Aceh">Banda Aceh</a> who were affected by the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">2004 Indian Ocean Tsunami</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> He produced the single "We Can Make It Better" by Don Asian with <a href="/wiki/Mukhtar_Sahota" title="Mukhtar Sahota">Mukhtar Sahota</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In 2008 Rahman opened the <a href="/wiki/KM_Music_Conservatory" title="KM Music Conservatory">KM Music Conservatory</a> with an audio-media education facility to train aspiring musicians in vocals, instruments, music technology and sound design. The conservatory (with prominent musicians on staff and a symphony orchestra) is located near his studio in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kodambakkam,_Chennai" title="Kodambakkam, Chennai">Kodambakkam, Chennai</a> and offers courses at several levels. Violinist <a href="/wiki/L._Subramaniam" title="L. Subramaniam">L. Subramaniam</a> is on its advisory board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rahmankm_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rahmankm-151">[151]</a></sup> Several of Rahman's proteges from the studio have scored feature films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> He composed the theme music for a 2006 short film for <a href="/wiki/The_Banyan_(NGO)" title="The Banyan (NGO)">The Banyan</a> to aid poor women in Chennai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008 Rahman and noted percussionist <a href="/wiki/Sivamani" title="Sivamani">Sivamani</a> created a song, "Jiya Se Jiya", inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Free_Hugs_Campaign" title="Free Hugs Campaign">Free Hugs Campaign</a> and promoted it with a video filmed in a number of Indian cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
